Page 14

Free Talk

Old Sayings

— Yu

If we remove the blindfold from the eyes of religious figures, we can know that the God or deities worshiped by religious figures are not the protectors of humanity. If deities are the personification of nature, then humanity is in opposition to nature. This concept of opposition existed in the early legends of various nations.

According to the early legends of various nations, the earliest rulers were always gods, or beings between gods and humans, or descendants of gods. And the majority of those who revered the gods were created by the gods from special materials. In Hebrew lore, God created man from dust; in Chinese mythology, Nuwa molded humans from yellow earth; and among the Seminoles and Choctaw tribes of North America, there is a myth of the "God of Life" creating humans from mud. These inferior beings, less valuable than "straw dogs," created by the gods, naturally exist or are eliminated according to the whims of the creator. In ancient times, there may have actually been a worldwide flood, hence the widespread flood legends among various peoples. All religious figures use these legends as material for their preaching. The Old Testament says: "The Lord saw that the wickedness of man was great in the earth, and that every intent of the thoughts of his heart was only evil continually. The Lord regretted that He had made man on the earth, and He was grieved in His heart. The Lord said, 'I will destroy man whom I have created from the face of the earth...'" Among the TupjGuaran tribe of South America, there is a similar story: the creator god Monan felt that humanity was too bad, so he decided to destroy the world with fire. The great wizard Irin Mape, in order to save humanity, sent rain to extinguish the fire, resulting in a devastating flood. In Aeschylus's tragedy Prometheus Bound, there is also such a story, saying that Zeus intended to destroy humanity and create a new race. Prometheus, this giant, out of love for humanity, stole fire and gave it to humanity, thus incurring Zeus's wrath and being chained to the rocks of the Caucasus.

All these legends show that humans and nature are standing in opposition, with no room for reconciliation. Either humans use nature and conquer it, or humans are conquered by nature and destroyed by it. Therefore, the ideal world envisioned by those who advocate a return to nature or harmony with nature: "In the age of highest virtue, their actions are simple and honest, their vision is straightforward; all things grow together, quickly returning to their origin, birds and beasts form herds, and plants grow tall. Therefore, birds and beasts can be tethered and roam; birds and magpies' nests can be climbed and disturbed..." is by no means a paradise. The Garden of Eden where Adam and Eve lived, as described in the Old Testament's Book of Genesis, is merely a deceptive allegory of religious figures. On the contrary, the fact that Eve, the female ancestor of humanity, was tempted by the serpent, picked the fruit of wisdom, and ate it with Adam, thus "their eyes were opened," and for this reason they were expelled from the Garden of Eden and "in toil shall you eat of it all the days of your life," precisely illustrates the upward progress of humanity, and by no means its fall. Therefore, the lines Milton laments for Adam and Eve in Paradise Lost:

"Earth trembled from her entrails, as again

In pangs, and Nature gave a second groan;

Sky loured, and, muttering thunder, some sad drops

Wept at completing of the mortal Sin Original..."

We can also say the opposite: the trembling of the earth, the groaning of nature, and the lowering of the sky are precisely the fear of all nature towards humanity's conquest of it, and not the fear of nature for humanity's sin. The inevitable demise of a world ruled by gods and the gods' fear of humanity was already felt by the preachers of the gods. The old Book of Genesis says: After the flood, "Now the whole world had one language and a common speech. As people moved eastward, they found a plain in Shinar and settled there. They said to each other, 'Come, let's make bricks and bake them thoroughly.' They used brick instead of stone, and tar for mortar. Then the said, 'Come, let us build ourselves a city, with a tower that reaches to the heavens, so that we may make a name for ourselves; otherwise we will be scattered over the face of the whole earth.' But the Lord came down to see the city and the tower the people were building. The Lord said, 'If as one people speaking the same language they have begun to do this, then nothing they plan to do will be impossible for them. Come, let us go down and confuse their language so they will not understand each other.' So the Lord scattered them from there over all the earth, and they stopped building the city."

This meaning precisely illustrates the power that nature exerts on humanity and humanity's attempts to conquer nature.

In the same sense, in the aforementioned Greek tragedy Prometheus Bound, Prometheus, the protector of humanity, in order to protect humanity, taught people to build houses, to recognize the seasons, to understand production, to create writing, to plow with oxen, to acquire medical knowledge, to unite, and to use iron, metals, etc., to resist the power of nature. Weak humanity obtained such weapons, and one day they will overthrow the master of the universe, the newly emerging tyrant Zeus, from that glorious throne.

Aeschylus had two other tragedies with the same character as the protagonist that have now been lost, one called The Fire-Giver and Prometheus Unbound. It is said that in the latter play, Prometheus did not meet his predestined fate, as described in Prometheus Bound, and perish, but Prometheus himself finally reconciled with Zeus. The English poet Shelley was not very satisfied with such an ending. So he also created a poetic drama called Prometheus Unbound. In the preface to this play, Shelley said: "I am very disgusted with the ending of the protector of humanity reconciling with the oppressor of humanity. The moral significance of this fable is supported by Prometheus's suffering and patience. If we think that he submitted to his enemy, that meaning is completely eliminated." Therefore, in his play, Zeus finally walks towards his fate of destruction, and humanity also finally reaches the "classless realm" of "unrestricted equality, freedom of the idol." In this way, in Shelley's play, there is another meaning existing.

A Sleepless Night (Part 1)

— Long Zaitian

Ke Liangfu, because of his neurasthenia for two months, moved to Town T, sixty miles outside the city, for convalescence. Town T is famous for its hot springs, and most people who have never been there would probably imagine a beautiful and picturesque scenery. But in fact: the mountains are so small that it may take less than ten minutes to go around them, and it is a barren, bald mountain; the northern part does have more than a hundred black pines, but they were planted not long ago and have not yet provided shade; the houses are so simple; the streets are so deserted and messy...

The place where Ke Liangfu lives also does not have electric lights installed. Coupled with the annoyance that summer night country mosquitoes inflict on people, it is quite alarming. Therefore, before the long black night had completely occupied the position of dusk, he quietly climbed into his solitary bedroom and lay down.

When he first got into bed, he was quite tired, and it seemed like a good dream would follow. Because during the long summer, he had never slept a nap, especially recently. In order to seek a sweet slumber, he always took a solitary walk for about an hour before and after the mountains at dusk, which was indeed a bit exhausting. But as soon as he closed his eyes, inexplicably, as usual, all the unpleasant thoughts, like the annoying mosquitoes outside the tent, flew together again.

At first, he was still calm, deliberately scratching his cheek leisurely, scratching his ears, looking at the top of the tent, and sometimes thinking about some of his proud deeds in his life to suppress these unpleasant thoughts. However, because he was still young, there were too few proud deeds. In less than a few minutes, this momentary joy withered like a ephemera, and he still held the city of sadness of ten thousand hu, so he turned over. Sometimes he also thought of memories close to debauchery; sometimes he even thought of fantasies that might be extremely far away. However, what he could not resist was the fact that the pale face of his mother, who was worried and unhappy everywhere after his eldest brother and third sister had an accident and misfortune, also flashed before his eyes. Turning over is like the mosquitoes flying a little farther after being driven away, but flying back again in a moment!

And at this time, his thoughts were really stuck in a dead end, no matter how hard he struggled, he could not get out. Outside the room: Kang Yu and Li Meina had also been lying down for a long time. And Kang Yu, before turning off the lights, habitually called out to him in a Sichuan accent, teasingly:

"Ke Liangfu is still playing dead? Really asleep?"

He was afraid that once he answered, it would further stimulate the excitement of his nerves, so he also habitually answered him with silence. But he could not help but feel a burst of irritability, and then he also habitually began to count the numbers one two three four five... Although he also knew it was ineffective.

Manufacture

Insult

— Zhou Lengjia

The streetcar rang its bell, "ding-ding," and stopped at a platform. Lin, carrying her silk umbrella and purse, got off the streetcar.

The broadcasting from a wireless radio in a store across the street caught her attention. She looked up and saw her beautiful face reflected clearly in the mirror embedded in the display window. Her face was flushed with anger, and a few beads of sweat dotted her forehead.

Instinctively, Lin took out her handkerchief and wiped the sweat from her forehead. At the same time, the impression from that brief moment on the streetcar reappeared before her eyes.

It was truly outrageous! How could people see the position of women in society as so low? Did women not have independent personalities and were instead meant to be played with by the masses? She felt that those few minutes on the streetcar were an unforgettable humiliation in her life.

The story was this: In the morning, she had accidentally broken her only washbasin in the dormitory. Moreover, the towel she often used was also somewhat dirty and old. She also needed to replenish several daily necessities and cosmetics. For these reasons, Lin, who usually disliked going out, had no choice but to venture out to make purchases.

The weather was unusually hot, and the asphalt on the road was melting in the sun. The rickshaw pullers took the opportunity to raise the price of their labor. A short distance was being quoted at more than two dimes, which Lin, limited by her financial circumstances, could not afford. To save some money, she had to hold her silk umbrella and walk to the streetcar stop, which was over a hundred steps away from her school.

Standing under the scorching sun, waiting for the distant streetcar to arrive, was a very uncomfortable experience. Finally, she managed to see the car arrive, but the people getting on and off were extremely crowded. Lin patiently waited for everyone to board before stepping onto the streetcar steps. At this moment, the car bell rang, and the car started moving. Lin jumped up with all her might, but failed to get on, making her very anxious. Fortunately, the ticket seller standing by the car door pulled her arm, finally pulling her onto the car. Initially, she was very grateful to him, but when she looked up and saw the ticket seller's grinning mouth and the passengers' strange smiles, she realized that she had been taken advantage of. This unexpected insult made her angry, but what could she do? She could only barely endure it and walk into the carriage.

The carriage was already packed, with people even hanging from the rattan loops. Lin had to lean against the car door, and her legs, which had been standing for a long time, gradually felt unable to support her. At this moment, a young man in a smart suit suddenly stood up and offered her his seat. Lin accepted his kindness without hesitation and gave him a grateful glance. She thought that there were still a few polite people among the Chinese.

This young man stood in front of Lin, his eyes constantly glancing at her face. Lin didn't pay attention and proceeded to take out money to buy a ticket. But gradually, she felt something was wrong. She felt a heavy pressure on her knees. A lewd smile tempted her; it was the young man who had given her the seat. At the same time, when the ticket seller handed her the ticket, he intentionally or unintentionally touched her fingers. All these insults filled her with anger. Without saying a word, she jumped up and stood again, letting the car shake her body to her destination.

Past impressions unfolded one by one before Lin's eyes. Deep sorrow bit into her heart like a snake. She thought that the slogans of the women's movement had been shouted in China for over a decade, but they still could not change the condescending and playful attitude of people in society towards women. Whose fault was this? She regretted not being willing to spend the extra money and take a rickshaw.

But the past was already in the past. Besides suffering some insults, there was no real loss, so there was no need to think about it anymore. So, she calmed down and walked into the store.

The electric fan turned briskly above her head, and a cool breeze blew over her body. All her anger was blown away by the wind, and her spirits rose again. She patiently looked carefully for the items she needed, moving from one counter to another. A delicately designed electric jade container caught her eye. She couldn't help but pick out a washbasin from it and asked the male clerk behind the counter:

"Hey! How much does this sell for?"

"Fifty-six cents!" the clerk said in a frivolous tone, while making a face at Lin.

Lin hesitated. Spending so much money on a washbasin seemed too extravagant. But looking closely at the delicate container, she couldn't bear to put it down. So, she ventured to try bargaining.

"Will you sell it for thirty cents?"

"Hmph! Thirty cents? You can only buy... haha!..." The clerk laughed lightly and turned to another clerk beside him, who also laughed strangely.

Lin couldn't help but become furious. Daring to use such a rogue tone towards a customer, and especially a young woman, was unacceptable. She really wanted to slap the clerk twice across the face. But seeing the people around her and thinking that she was just a woman, and could not win against others in any way, she had to swallow her anger and put down the washbasin, walking out of the store.

Finally, she bought what she needed in a store with female clerks. Although the female clerk's face was very cold when she made the transaction, Lin felt much more at ease. She sighed softly, feeling that this day of humiliation and suffering had finally come to an end.

Also Lili's Gaze

— Jiadi

Wrapped in a lonely dusk,

Drawing thin, long, faint shadows.

This line of coconut trees,

Stands resolutely,

Playing the melody of a group of iron men.

A few strands of speechless evening breeze

A city of hazy night, quietly,

Where does a melancholy posture come from?

That—

Is the eyebrow of the new moon

That—

Is also Lili's gaze.

University Days (33)

— Written by Storm of Germany, translated by Chen Yin

I don't know why I was startled when I heard this. I was about to ask this braggart more, but suddenly remembered that I had seen lame Mary sitting in the landlord's side room when I went out just now.

I immediately set off for home, and half an hour later I was standing beside her talking to her.

"Haven't you seen Lena Li for a long time?" I asked.

She was silent for a while. "I don't do needlework with her anymore," she said, her eyes fixed on her work.

"You used to be good friends!"

"Used to be, yes!"—She rubbed the newly sewn lines with her fingernail for a while. "But since she danced with the university students in the suburbs.... He is not often at the old aunt's house now; I'm afraid the will will also be changed."

"Oh, so that's what happened!" I thought—Christopher sent back the borrowed money shortly after he left, with a few simple words saying that he was very popular in his uncle's house, and the old couple and their middle-aged daughter liked him, and he was very busy with work.

Since then I have not heard from him or Nali.

"But, how could this happen?" I asked again after a while, while the seamstress was busy with her needlework.

"It's like this!" she said, inserting the needle into the clothes. "Two weeks before Pentecost, Nali was already annoyed; at first I thought it was because the carpenter hadn't written to her for a long time, but sometimes I felt as if this marriage made her uncomfortable, and she didn't seem to know what to do. She often lost her temper and didn't care about offending me or the noble customers: especially when she heard the music in the dance hall, she lost her temper even more, because she had promised the carpenter not to go to the dance hall again. One evening we were sitting on the bench at my door, and my nephew and a few buddies came to my house to chat. He is a tailor and just returned from abroad the day before. He had traveled to the Rhine River area and worked in two or three cities there; he said the names of these cities, but I forgot them. Other buddies asked him, and he talked about it.—'Have you seen Christopher, Werner?' someone asked.—'The carpenter? I did see him; he is having good luck.'—'What's good?' another asked.—'What's good? He married the master's daughter; she has... you understand what I mean?' He made a gesture as if counting lines. I felt very sad when I heard this. 'Child, wake up!' I said, 'What are you talking about!'—'Duh, aunt, I am very awake!' he shouted, 'I was still next to him when he was planing the board to make his wedding bed!'——Nali heard this, stood up from the bench without saying a word, took her hat, and walked down the street without looking back. 'What sad thing happened to her?' my nephew asked. —'I don't know, Dietrich.'—I really didn't know. She and the carpenter were not very enthusiastic, because he had been chasing her for a long time, and she had considered it twice before promising. Although I already knew about her and that noble young master, that university student, I never thought that he would completely confuse her stubborn mind like this.

'I sat with them for a while, listening to the child, the carpenter, tell some stories; but I only listened with half an ear, and soon I couldn't bear it anymore, because I was very concerned about her.

Shanghai Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Ping City Bans Renting Wives

— Qiong Sheng

A special dispatch from Beiping on the 24th stated: "The city government recently learned from a report on the 22nd that there is an evil trend of renting wives in Ping City. If true, it is extremely detrimental to public morals. Today, the Public Security Bureau was instructed to direct its subordinates to pay close attention and conduct strict investigations and bans."

The evil trend of renting wives in China, I think, is by no means "news" that has only been "discovered" today. Not long ago, Shanghai newspapers published a communication from the provincial capital of Guizhou, saying how prevalent this trend is there, and the facts of how much money it costs to rent for a year and how much money it costs to rent for a month. In Beiping, as I know from my years of living there, this matter has indeed been embellishing our "sunset of the ancient city" old capital. If you go to the surrounding towns or the Tianqiao area to investigate, there is also a kind of "deceiving superiors but not inferiors" market quotation for the rental of wives. The Chinese have always been accustomed to wearing high hats and building temples, looking down at the world with squinting eyes, how can they see through this hell-like situation; even the general scholars and gentlemen, when they arrive in Beiping, only know how majestic and secluded the three palaces and three seas are. These things are seen by them without knowing, and known without speaking.

So why did this trend suddenly spread to the newspapers and cause the authorities to strictly ban it? Readers probably still remember that since Luandong became a war zone and the rogues ran rampant, many "societies" have been formed accordingly, and they are about to start the business of "pawning children" and "mortgaging women." There is an old Chinese saying that there are no intact eggs under a capsized nest. After a period of panic in northern China, it seemed that Ping City had entered the same situation. The problem is very clear. When pawning children and buying sons and daughters is forced to grow secretly, why wouldn't the "evil trend of renting wives" prevail under the same reason? Even close flesh and blood must be separated. How can we talk to them about morality and shame.

Regarding this matter, we don't want to extend it to discuss the women's issue, because discussing women's liberation in this matter itself is equivalent to a kind of literary game. The central issue lies in how to eliminate the root cause of renting wives. Of course, this root cause has its own root cause. As long as everyone treats others as they would like to be treated, no one wants to rent their wife to others, but they themselves wear a "green hat" in vain. If "renting wives" is strictly prohibited with "morality" as the focus, this is tantamount to advising people, "It doesn't matter if a 'true man' starves to death," but he must never wear a "green hat." Therefore, as soon as the ordinance is implemented, many people who wear "green hats" can temporarily "not rent their wives" for fear of power, but under the pressure of hunger and cold, how can they guarantee that they will not change from long-term "rental" to short-term sale? But in this way, I don't know what is called "morality," how will it survive, and where will it not harm morality.

Riverside

— Da Yun

The yellow sandy river, here it is particularly narrow, the tide rushes down from a high place, whirlpools are swirling on the water, and white waves are splashing high.

The embankment is wet. The green grass can no longer withstand trampling, showing a declining state. Groups of shepherd boys, sitting sideways on the backs of cows, whistle lightly, and some raise their voices and sing popular folk songs in the village, heading towards the villages with rows of houses emitting curling smoke.

The horizon is full of red clouds, which do not look like the afterglow of the setting sun. A cool breeze blows in gusts, and swarms of red dragonflies fly towards the other shore along the wind. Sensible adults, everyone expects unfortunate things to happen to them, unlike those young lads, who still sing joyful tunes, harbor a gloating mood, and spend their days carefree.

Blood-red clouds, yellow muddy river water, with a cool and humid wind, swarms of red dragonflies... these, in the eyes of experienced people, are originally omens of floods.

The river water is only a few feet away from the embankment. Undoubtedly, the disaster of water is possible. Based on everyone's past experience, if the sky rains again and the upstream mountain torrents break out, and the fierce water flow pours down, the embankment will inevitably be breached. Then, the crops cultivated so hard for months will be flooded by the overflowing torrents. So, the autumn harvest that the farmers have been looking forward to will turn into nothing. Looking at the swirling river in the heart of the river, the white waves splashing, everyone's mind is imprinted with the ghostly shadow of this terrible flood.

"The God of Heaven really intends to make fun of us farmers!" Brother Xiuqin looked up at the red sunset in the sky and murmured with emotion.

"Isn't it? Last year, the fields were so dry that they were cracked, and the seedlings were scorched and hung down to the ground in rolls. No matter how we invited the Dragon King, promised a bunch of three-seven-one and piously prayed, he still refused to rain. It's really his mother's..." Grandpa Xiong, who was full of vigor, although he was not young, always spoke with a bit of wildness and anger. He was not afraid of the sky—since last year he had not trusted the gods, the Dragon King, this kind of vague bodhisattva. He did not believe that cursing the sky and the bodhisattva would lead to any "sin" and be punished.

Thinking of the drought last year, Grandpa Xiong's chest suddenly felt as if a sharp knife was inserted into it! He had lived so many days, and had never seen a drought as fierce and terrible as last year! There was also a drought more than ten years ago. Although there was no thin porridge to eat at that time, at least wild water chestnuts and grass roots were enough to get by. But in last year's drought, even tree bark and tree roots were peeled off and dug up. Then, the plague spread and raged in the village. Every day, people in the village were packed into thin wooden boxes and carried to the desolate tombs outside the village; his wife and son, under the wings of this plague that had no bloody smell and yet killed people without batting an eye, were taken to heaven, leaving him alone.

Looking at the surging river water full of yellow mud, and listening to the leisurely and seductive frivolous folk songs that wafted out of the mouths of the shepherd boys sitting sideways on the backs of cows, this made a raging flame burst out of Grandpa Xiong's heart. He cursed angrily: "You unkillable wild things, you simply don't know how to die and you're still singing your mother's fart song! When the flood comes, don't expect to have tree bark and tree roots to fill your belly. Big fish are waiting for your floating corpses. Humph, wild things who don't know how to die! Still singing your mother's fart song!"

In the northwest corner of the sky, clusters of black clouds tumbled, quickly swallowing the fiery red sunset. Lightning flashed in the black clouds, carving golden snakes, and thunder rumbled faintly. "It's going to rain again up there." Leaning his head, he said to Brother Xiuqin: "The flood is inevitable, alas, everything is over!" Grandpa Xiong looked at the swirling eddies and splashing waves on the water and sighed blankly.

Page 16

Moving

— Mou Mu

A person, traveling alone in a foreign land, for the sake of life and environment, his residence is just like floating duckweed on the water, without a fixed place. And renting a house from someone else is also full of unspeakable troubles and inconveniences. Often, because of other people's likes and dislikes, or because of one's own reasons, one has to sulk and pout to move east and west. Although I am not yet qualified to establish a "home," just moving these few boxes, beds, tables, and some scattered things, books, and the like is enough to cause a headache.

After settling in a house, I often feel that the things I need daily are always lacking this or not prepared that. For a small cardboard box or a small nail, I often get annoyed and swear, and it is also common to complain a lot to myself. However, although I usually feel that there are too few things to use, once I move, I feel that there are too many useless things to move, such as paper, cardboard boxes, small bottles, broken shoes, and rotten boxes. As a result, a large batch of waste is discarded. Sometimes, for the sake of calculating transportation costs, tables, chairs, and iron beds have to be discarded. Although I feel very distressed, there is nothing I can do.

Now I have to move again.—I am not qualified enough to say "moving home"—but where to move to? This is difficult for me again. The alley houses in Shanghai are not something I dare to experience in this hot weather; still in Jiangwan, but it is really too difficult to find a place with tap water for me to wash. What's more, I want a building? Under the scorching sun, I ran all day with sweat on my head, and when I came back, I could only lie on the messy bed and sigh. The days are almost over. After seeing off the friends who went home, looking at the messy room: the empty bookshelves, the torn wallpaper, the dusty tables and chairs, I really feel anxious and desolate. I didn't expect this small moving problem to disturb my heart so much!

In the morning, the landlord had already come to inform me that the new tenants would move in this afternoon. But I'm still going in circles! I have learned a little bit of cunning after living in Shanghai for a few years. I know that Shanghai's worldly affairs are not built on "friendship"; in order not to be looked down upon, it is better to be sensible. I made a decision and spent a whole morning moving to this new residence.

Although the house is a newly built small foreign house, living on the ground floor, there are many poisonous mosquitoes in the countryside. In this way, it is really impossible for me to write under the lamp. During the day, there is either the heart-rending crying or the children's shouting. However, this place is still considered the best choice. I can't be picky anymore, because I am poisoned by hygiene and I am used to taking a bath every day. This place just has tap water for me to use.

Regarding a new residence, no matter how satisfactory it is beforehand, in the first few days after moving in, I always feel unfamiliar and unaccustomed. What's more, I am no longer living in a house that I own. For example, when using boiling water, I have to wait until the servants of others are done. As a result, I often have to take a thermos to the teahouse to make it. If I weren't hungry, I really wouldn't be happy to wear shoes and socks to the restaurant for lunch every day. Now I continue to know that I have a comfort of having a cook to supply meals. Thinking that there are still two long months of summer, I really don't know what to do.

What makes me even more uncomfortable here is the radio that is never tired of playing every night. Naturally, being able to play one or two sets of Western music, or more noble and beautiful Chinese music, is also quite pleasing to the ears; and the buzzing chanting sound that starts early in the morning is probably when the landlady is sincerely worshiping Buddha. However, the Shanghai people's understanding of business can also be seen from this.

The house is finally settled, although there are many shortcomings. Unless I have to move away in the future, I plan to adopt a wait-and-see attitude and muddle through; life has decided that I can only rent other people's houses to live in, and it is difficult to find things that completely meet my ideals, and I really don't have the courage to enjoy the troubles caused by moving.

Untitled

— Simon

The several people who lived with me have all left one after another. The pointless annoyances that used to make me feel extremely disgusted have also gone with them. I suddenly feel a burst of lightness, like the kind of lightness one feels running out of a turbulent and long-depressed theater. For almost the past month, I've been detached from the pen that I rely on to make a living. It can certainly be said that this is because the weather is excessively hot, making it impossible to even live, let alone engage in the mentally exhausting task of racking my brains. But it is also because the environment does not allow me even an hour or even a moment of quiet contemplation. This is truly difficult. Just as I was laboriously gestating a drop of thought, preparing for the time when my arm could comb it out, those frivolous housemates who spent their days idly chatting or telling vulgar stories would either erupt in loud laughter or suddenly raise their voices in a noisy melee. Perhaps someone would even pat me on the shoulder from behind, pulling me into their meaningless chatter. Although I showed no interest, their interest was naturally strong. And at that moment, that drop of thought had already quietly drifted away. I had no choice but to helplessly put down my pen and stand up in frustration. Perhaps I would simply slip out the door because their vulgar faces, even if I sat silently, would provoke unwarranted disgust and even unwarranted anger. For the past month, the pen and ink bottle have lain motionless on the table, covered in a thick layer of dust. Now that they are gone, this huge house is left to me alone. I can keep the door tightly shut and no longer worry about who might be knocking, as those knockers have also vanished with them. Even if I occasionally hear a knock or two, I can pretend that no one is home and ignore it. In this way, the tranquility I have been yearning for is gradually approaching, and it should be time to start the writing that needs to be done in silence. I am determined to replant the long-barren inkstone field, but after these days of becoming a wild horse, the excessively active heart is a little difficult to restrain. Everything feels strangely unfamiliar, as if the pen in my hand has become as heavy as a bamboo pole. My brain is like a rusty, long-abandoned machine, unable to produce even a ripple of thought. What can I do? When I wanted to write, I could not find a suitable environment, but now that I have a suitable environment, I cannot stir up any inspiration. I sigh with disappointment as I face the blank paper. And in this solitary mood that I cherish, I am often too mindful of the only sounds in the silence, the chirping of a cicada or the croaking of a frog. During the long and tedious days of summer, from the moment the sun rises, the cicada hides in the shade of green leaves, chirping rhythmically. If I happen to be brewing some literary thoughts, the noisy cicada will immediately steal away my original inspiration and give rise to a different idea and mood. And from the moment this short-lived little creature's song is clear and loud, to when it becomes stagnant, and then to when it becomes choked, I seem to hear the sound of time galloping by, passing from one season to another, reminding me that many things, many things, will fade away like the fading sound of the cicada.

Similarly, what can derail my thoughts at night, besides the distant, desolate sound of a sharp train whistle, is the noisy croaking of frogs in the shallow pond behind the house. Listening to it, it seems to carry an almost desolate meaning. Because it is late at night, and the surroundings are silent and still, the croaking of the frogs is extremely clear and piercing. If it is after rain, then it will be even denser, like a sudden rainstorm. The croaking of the frogs can easily disturb my mind, often making me leave my seat and stuff the spread-out manuscript paper into the drawer, or even turn off the light. Sleep is out of the question. I walk near the window, looking at the dark sky. There is no moon, only sparse stars shining with cold eyes. Listening to the frogs croaking more diligently, in this hazy, confused, dark night, the life of the frog does not seem insignificant, but full of boundless loneliness. And I am not bothered by the frog's croaking that keeps me awake. What worries me is that my thoughts are too colorful, simply impossible to collect. When will I find a topic?

When the Great Flood Comes

— Erlang

Uncle He, panting, stepped into his own house. Looking around, the house was quiet and empty, with not a single person in sight. Only the cat was playing upside down on the table in the main room, using its four legs to claw at the air.

"Xiao Niu's mother, Xiao Niu's mother!... Damn it, where did you go?" He shouted, but no one answered, and he started cursing.

Xiao Niu's mother—Aunt He—was at this time in the backyard, tidying up the firewood and rice straw that had been soaked by the continuous rain. She spread out the firewood and rice straw in the yard to dry in the sun, muttering, "All soaked through, all soaked through!" She did not hear Uncle He's voice from the front. Uncle He searched to the back and, seeing Aunt He's leisurely mood, an idea floated into his mind: "Still drying these birds!" He shouted loudly at Aunt He, one might even say scolding her, "Hurry up, the great flood is coming! Pack things and go upstairs!" Saying this, he turned around and went into the house to move things.

The great flood is coming? Aunt He had heard this news this morning but did not believe it would come so quickly; at the same time, recalling the terrible situation when the water came three years ago, she was stunned. Uncle He had already moved a box upstairs from the house and still did not see her come. "Damn it, what are you doing in the back?" He rushed out and shouted loudly, "Come quickly, you'll die in the back!" Only then did Aunt He seem to wake up from a dream, taking two steps for every three, hobbling into the house.

Aunt He was not a capable woman, and she was usually beaten and scolded by Uncle He because of her clumsiness. At this time, hearing "The great flood is coming!" her soul seemed to have left her body for the most part, and she did not know what to pack in the house. Although she also went to busy herself, taking this and taking that, sweat flowed down her face, and she often wiped it with her sleeves, but after Uncle He had moved the chest upstairs, when he wanted to go to the main room to pick up the grain, he turned around and saw that she was filling a small bamboo box with broken shoes and rags from under the bed! This could not but make Uncle He angry, and he shouted at her, "What are you doing? You don't pack the clothes, what's the use of taking those broken things? Damn it, get out, go into the river!"

Aunt He then seemed to awaken and also felt it was funny, why had she packed the broken shoes and rags from under the bed? She grabbed the broken shoes and rags out of the small bamboo box and busily stuffed them back under the bed where they originally were. She got on the bed and picked up Xiao Niu's clothes, Uncle He's clothes, and her own clothes and broken cotton blankets, and climbed down from the bed. After walking a few steps, she was stunned again. She was about to stuff them into the small bamboo box, but the cotton blanket was too big, and the small bamboo box could not fit it. She was about to take it upstairs, but she bumped into Uncle He, carrying a large basket of grain on his back, humming and carefully walking to the wooden ladder; so she put the cotton blanket on the ground next to the ladder, and then rushed to the bed to get the clothes. The bed was an old-fashioned one, a treasure passed down from generations of ancestors, both wide and large. She climbed inside to take out the clothes, but when she was about to put them in the small bamboo box, she looked at them and saw that they were a messy pile, so she thought, "The clothes in the box should be folded well," and put them on the edge of the bed, folding each piece neatly, and then putting each piece into the small bamboo box.

Uncle He had carried all seven or eight baskets of grain in the main room upstairs, but Aunt He's clothes were not yet packed, and the sound of gongs came from outside. Interspersed with the words: "Everyone go to the dike to defend it!" Uncle He was anxious. Seeing her slowly folding clothes, he rushed forward and slapped her, "Damn it, why aren't you faster!" Aunt He took a step back to dodge, but had already taken a slap in the face: she habitually started to cry and make a fuss. She simply stopped packing her clothes. Uncle He, with fierce eyes and a stern face, pointed at her and said, "I'll see if you don't hurry up, I'll beat you again!" Saying this, he ran out of the house to defend the dike. Just as he reached the door, Xiao Niu ran in from outside with a smile, calling "Mom" all the way, "The great flood is coming, it's already on the dike!" Uncle He knew it was critical and said to his son, "Help your mom pack things and go upstairs, I'm going to defend the dike." He also said: "Don't come, you little rascal!"

Fatty Guan Turns Pencils from His Navel

On the day the "Kaige" sound film "Chunsheng's Doorway" was being shot, the actors included Yuan Meiyun, Wang Guilin, Wei Heling, Wang Yin, Fatty Guan Hongda, and Jiang Xiu. After shooting four scenes, it was lunchtime. After everyone was full, they sat in the shade of the green trees to rest and chat. Fatty Guan had a large stomach and a large appetite. Others had finished eating and left the dining hall, but he was still devouring greedily, until he had eaten nine large bowls of rice. Only then did he hum the love song sung by Yuan Meiyun in "Kaige," shaking his head and swaying his hips as he walked out of the dining hall. Yuan Meiyun saw him and asked, "Fatty, how many bowls of rice did you eat today?" "The weather is too hot today," Fatty replied, "I only ate nine bowls of rice."

"Nine bowls of rice is still too little? Oh my gosh!" Meiyun stuck out her bright red tongue in surprise. "Let me tell you, don't be afraid, I've eaten twelve bowls. When I was an anti-Japanese volunteer in the Northeast, I ate thirty large steamed buns in one meal."

"Oh! Fatty, your navel is really big," Meiyun pointed at Fatty's hairy big navel that was exposed outside, and said.

"Big is not strange, what's strange is that it can do magic," Fatty said proudly, "Does anyone want to see magic?"

"Yes, we want to see, we want to see..."

Fatty imitated the demeanor of a magician, gesturing with his hands and feet, sometimes forward and sometimes backward, panting and sighing, sweat pouring down like rain. Suddenly, he shouted, "Come out!" He thrust his stomach forward, and a pencil more than an inch long flew out of his navel. Cheers and applause rang out like thunder. Someone picked up the pencil and returned it to Fatty, who stuffed it back into his navel, causing everyone to exclaim in surprise, dumbfounded. Director Wan Cang was satisfied and rewarded him with two bottles of soda. In an instant, the clock struck, and it was time to shoot. "Kaige" continued shooting.

Shenbao Architectural Weekly

Japanese Temple Architecture

— Ito Chuta (Author), Zhang Guangzheng (Translator)

As the author of this article says, religious architecture is indeed a leader in the architectural world, guiding other architecture. Looking at countries with long cultural histories such as China, Greece, Rome, and India, the architectural art that has endured and still maintains a considerable position in the architectural world is mostly represented by churches and temples. Moreover, modern architectural styles are greatly influenced by them.

Japanese temple architecture also occupies a very important position in Eastern architectural art. The author of this article is a famous Japanese temple architecture expert. From this article, we can get a general understanding of Japanese temple architecture. (Translator)

Religious Architecture and Non-Religious Architecture

In the West, architecture has long been divided into two categories: one is religious architecture and the other is non-religious architecture. Religious architecture is indeed a leader in the architectural world, guiding other architecture. In Japan, it used to be like this, especially Buddhist temples, which maintained the dignity of the throne of the architectural world. But today, due to the decline of religion, the dignity of this type of architecture has been lost accordingly. It has only become a province of the architectural kingdom, to the point where it cannot but be compared with general non-religious buildings such as government offices, schools, public halls, large companies, theaters, factories, and houses. This is a common phenomenon in the world due to the historical trend and the rapid advancement of non-religious architecture.

At the same time, people's methods of studying world religious architecture have changed. It is believed that temples, houses, government offices, factories, etc. are originally all buildings, and there is originally no distinction between superior and inferior. Now, it is felt that there is not much meaning in simply dividing architecture into religious and non-religious types. But now, based on what I (the author) have learned from this investigation, I will describe it in the following:

Here, the first question that needs to be considered is whether temples are religious. Regarding this question, people know that although it has been discussed for a long time, a clear answer has not yet been obtained. If religion is strictly and narrowly defined, then temples can be said not to be religious buildings; but if a broad interpretation is given, then temples can also be said to be religious buildings. Now, let us assume that temples exist because of religion. As for Buddhist temples, they are of course completely religious buildings, which is unnecessary to say. (To be continued)

Architectural History (II)

— Bu Ren

The Greeks seemed to possess very sensitive and well-trained eyes, so they did not like buildings whose style or proportions were not quite right. They created and completed three model architectural styles known as the "Three Orders" of column-and-beam construction—the first called Doric, the second Ionic, and the third Corinthian. Not only were the capitals of the columns very different, but the moldings and decorations also varied according to the architectural order, and the proportions were also different. Doric was the most plain and the most solid of the three. When the Greeks were conquered by the Romans, pure Greek architecture came to an end. The victorious Romans adopted many architectural designs from their new subjects, but they mixed these architectural designs entirely with their own.

The Romans were a very brave, enterprising, and practical people, not afraid of huge tasks, and often completing them in amazing ways. They were more interested in grandeur and magnificence than in aesthetic completeness. They often used clever methods to achieve huge effects at a cheap price and in a short amount of time, for example, covering houses made of brick or concrete with marble slabs, and decorating blank walls with columns and arches.

However, although the Romans often used such "tricks," they were ultimately excellent architects and superior builders; their great buildings still exist throughout Europe today.

They also had their own architectural order—in fact, three of them were somewhat imitated from the Greek architectural orders, and the fourth, the Composite order, can be said to be their own. Unlike the Greeks, they paid more attention to arches and domes.

From Roman buildings, we can get a glimpse of how they lived—first governed by a republic, then by an empire, from a period of hard work and high efficiency to a period of relaxation and luxury, and finally the disintegration of an empire that once dominated.

The capital, still owned by the Romans, was later moved from Rome to Byzantium (Constantinople), from which so-called Byzantine architecture developed. Brick was a material produced locally there, and they used it with excellent technique, especially for building domes. Roman domes had the same shape inside and out, which is one of the features that distinguishes Roman architecture from Greek architecture.

Then, Christians with even more power than before built many churches belonging to this architectural style; churches from before this period were simpler, based on old Roman courthouses, and most were built from columns and other materials collected from the ruins of Roman buildings. Similarly, soon after, natives living in the Roman Empire also began to build their own houses, using the remaining materials of dilapidated Roman buildings, or roughly imitating them.

With the development of Christianity, the construction of churches gradually increased, and the designs of these churches combined Byzantine and past Roman styles. The result of this mixture was the Romanesque architectural style that we call Byzantine. The Nordic style introduced to England, and the original Saxon style in England, were both products of variations of the Romanesque architectural style according to the location.

Like the original Roman buildings, these products of the Romanesque architectural style after changes also used a large amount of materials as a solid foundation for the buildings; however, from these architectural styles, a completely new architectural style called Gothic gradually developed. This is an architectural style that emphasizes ingenious balance over sturdy construction. Pointed arches and windows began to be used; light domes were supported by stone ribs: the lateral pressure of the arches and domes was balanced against each other to prevent them from breaking and moving. The builders of this period already understood the knowledge of engineering; they used this knowledge to make light materials create strong buildings. (The End)

The Completion of the Fence at Longhua Airport

The Longhua Airport of China National Aviation Corporation has recently merged with the airport of Eurasia Aviation Corporation to facilitate travel. The area for aircraft parking and part of the hangar were equipped with wire mesh fences this spring to form the outer perimeter. The total length of the fence is approximately 600 meters, and the entire fence is painted in colored paint, making it exceptionally beautiful. The surrounding protection has been greatly improved. At the same time, Eurasia Aviation Corporation also erected a movable mesh fence sliding gate with a length of approximately 150 feet at its Longhua air terminal. This type of sliding gate is the first installation of its kind in a Far Eastern air terminal. Rails are laid at the lower end, and the project is quite grand. It is reported that the above-mentioned fences and special gates were all manufactured by Shanghai Public Works Iron Works, and they also provided design and installation services. The work has been completely completed. In recent days, the road to Longhua has been crowded with travelers, and those who take the opportunity to visit the airport, upon seeing this brand-new facility, are amazed at the increasing advancement of material civilization.

From Architectural Art to the Temples of Greece (IV)

— Sun Zongwen

——The Most Glorious Page in the History of World Architecture——

(II) The Greek Temple and Capital Design

The appearance of capitals on Greek temples can be said to be a glorious miracle in the history of world architecture; it not only created a vital force in Greek architectural art at the time, but also contributed the greatest artistic crystallization to later architectural art. Therefore, we must give it a great description here. Originally, the evolution of Greek art can be divided into three periods:

(A) After the Inspiration period, the Doric Order appeared as a result. This type of capital was created by the Dorians. The middle of the column body is slightly larger and not very tall; the whole is mainly simple and thick, and is composed of a square plate Abacus, a round plate Echinus, and a round, light, continuous capital Neching, with no decoration; this is a product of the early stage of artistic evolution, so it is the oldest of all capitals and has survived to the present. The representative work of a temple using this capital is the Partheno Athens temple built on the Acropolis fortress; and it is also one of the most famous temples in the world, and its position in architectural art can be imagined.

Some people argue that the Doric capital evolved from wooden buildings, while others argue that it evolved from stone buildings—because the column body is very thick, wood cannot be used to make it, only stone is possible. The most temples of this type are in Greece, Holy, and Sicily.

(B) In the second period, the Ionic Order appeared. The column body is slender, with double discs at the bottom as a base, and the capital is decorated with spiral shapes, so it feels beautiful; the only representative work of a temple with this column is the Erechthion Athens temple built to the north of the Partheno temple, which is the most famous in the world, and the six columns on the south side of this temple are replaced by "Stone Goddess Columns," called Coryatids, which is the first discovery and application in Greek architectural history; therefore, the temple of this column is also a very valuable representative work in architectural history!

(C) In the third period, the fine parts of the column were extensively studied, so the products of this period were very exquisite and beautiful, maximizing the beauty, so the Cornithien Order appeared. This column emphasizes decoration, the column body is very slender, and the capital is carved with a lot of luxurious abandoned shapes (Acanthe's grass leaves). Its origin is a mixture of Egyptian columns and Aceling columns, and its shape is very similar to an inverted bell. According to a famous Roman architect, the first person to use this column did not use it on buildings, but on bronze objects, which was a pattern on a piece of copper on an ancient tomb, which was the first application of the Callinachus people on bronze, and it is also one of the sources of the pattern of this column. Although this column is very beautiful, it is no longer in line with the rational nature of the Greeks. The representative work of this column is the Olimpia Temple, in addition to which it is rarely used; because the style of this column is not in harmony with the Greek national character; fundamentally, Greek art is based on loyalty!

The above three types of capitals are widely used in modern great buildings, and in buildings with commemorative or artistic significance. If we go to the Bund along the Huangpu River for a stroll, we can prove that my words are not false.
